GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 35.01 ADMINISTRATIVE AND SERVICE FUNCTIONS CLASSIFIED INTO DEPARTMENTS.
   All administrative and service functions of the city are hereby classified
into the following departments established pursuant to KRS 83A.140 (6):
   (A)   Office Administration Department.
   (B)   Finance Department.
   (C)   Land Use Planning and Zoning Department.
   (D)   Police Department.
   (E)   Fire Department.
   (F)   Public Works Department.
   (G)   Public Utilities Department.
   (H)   Park and Recreation Department.
(Ord. 1-1-86, passed 1- -86)
§ 35.02 RESPONSIBILITIES OF DEPARTMENT HEADS.
   (A)   Subject to the budget therefor and the legislative, executive, and
administrative authority of the City Commission and all other laws and
regulations of any governmental agency having jurisdiction, the heads of the
departments established under §
35.01, other than the heads of the Fire Department, Public Utilities
Department, and the Parks and Recreation Department, shall have the duty and
responsibility for the general operation of the department which they head and
of the organization and supervision of the use of all funds, services, labor,
equipment, and material provided by the City Commission to accomplish the
functions described herein.
   (B)   The duty and responsibility of the heads of the Fire Department,
Public Utilities Department, and the Parks and Recreation Department shall be
limited to service as a liaison between the boards, commissions, or contractors
through which the functions of the department which they head are accomplished
pursuant to the provisions hereof. Periodic reports to the City Commission in
regard to the manner in which the functions of each of these three respective
departments are being accomplished and the compliance by such boards,
commissions, and contractors with the provisions of the ordinances and
contracts of the city and all laws, regulations, and orders of any other
governmental agency having jurisdiction shall also be provided.
(Ord. 1-1-86, passed 1- -86)
§ 35.03 RESPONSIBILITIES OF EMPLOYEES.
   The duties and responsibilities of the employees of each department
established under §
35.01, other than the Fire Department, Public Utilities Department, and the
Park and Recreation Department, shall be to accomplish the work assigned to
them by the head of the department in which they are employed or any authorized
delegate thereof, but subject to the legislative, executive, and administrative
authority of the City Commission and the laws and regulations of any other
governmental agency having jurisdiction. In the Fire Department, Public
Utilities Department, and Parks and Recreation Department, there shall be no
employees of the department; all employees therein shall be employees of the
board, commission, or contractor through which the functions of the department
are accomplished, and shall be subject to the authority thereof.
(Ord. 1-1-86, passed 1- -86)
POLICE DEPARTMENT
§ 35.15 ESTABLISHMENT; FUNCTIONS.
   Subject to the legislative, executive, and administrative authority of the
City Commission, all other laws and regulations of any other governmental
agency having jurisdiction, and the budget of the city, the function of the
Police Department shall be to provide for the enforcement of law and order
within the city; the prevention of criminal activity and the protection of all
persons and property within the city; and assistance in the prosecution of all
persons involved in any criminal activity in the city.
(Ord. 1-1-86, passed 1- -86)
§ 35.16 QUALIFICATIONS.
   The Police Department shall be composed of members who shall be appointed by
ordinance. Members shall be at least 21 years of age, and shall not have been
convicted of any offense that would be punishable as a felony under the laws of
the Commonwealth of Kentucky or any other state. Members shall have high
ethical character and shall conduct themselves in a manner free from
impropriety. They shall at no time conduct themselves in such a manner as to
bring discredit to the police or to the city. Any member hired after July 14,
1992, must be a high school graduate or have received general equivalency
diploma (G.E.D.).
Statutory reference:
   Qualifications, see KRS 95.710
§ 35.17 AUTHORITY TO CARRY CONCEALED DEADLY WEAPONS.
   (A)   Pursuant to the authorization of KRS 527.020, police officers of the
city are hereby expressly authorized to carry concealed deadly weapons on or
about their person at all times within the Commonwealth of Kentucky.
(Ord. 2-3-82, passed 4-8-82)
   (B)   Further, peace officers may carry concealed weapons on or about their
person when necessary for their protection in the discharge of their official
duties, in accordance with KRS 527.020.
§ 35.18 AUXILIARY POLICE FORCE.
   (A)   Pursuant to the authority of KRS 95.445, there is hereby established
an Auxiliary Police Force to perform special duties within the city.
   (B)   The Auxiliary Police Force shall be composed of no more than ten
members, each of whom shall be:
      (1)   Twenty-one years of age;
      (2)   A resident of the state;
      (3)   Honest, sober, and discreet, and of good reputation in the
community of his occupation and residence;
      (4)   Successful in the completion of standard physical and mental
examinations established and prescribed by the Chief of the Police Department;
and
      (5)   A graduate of an accredited high school or successful in the
completion of generally-recognized high school equivalency tests.
   (C)   The members of the Auxiliary Police Force shall be appointed by the
City Commission. Recommendations of the Chief of Police shall be taken into
consideration when making such appointments.
   (D)   Prior to engaging in any activity as a member of the Auxiliary Police
Force, each member shall take the oath required of police officers by state
law, and thereupon shall be considered to be peace officers of the city with
all of the powers, duties, and authority thereof. The exercise of such powers,
duties, and authority shall be limited to such locations, times, and
circumstances as are specifically designated by the Chief of Police; no member
of the Auxiliary Police Force shall act without such specific designation and
authorization by the Chief of Police.
   (E)   The function and duties of the Auxiliary Police Force shall be
supplementary to rather than in substitution for the function and duties of the
members of the Police Department. In the course thereof, the members of the
Auxiliary Police Force shall be subject to the direction, control, and
supervision of any member of the Police Department with whom any such member of
the Auxiliary Police Force is assigned to any activity.
   (F)   The members of the Auxiliary Police Force shall be subject to the
direct control and supervision of the Chief of Police who shall be responsible
for the operation of the Auxiliary Police Force under the general supervision
of the City Commission, and the training and activities of the members thereof.
There shall be no officers or rank within the membership of the Auxiliary
Police Force.
   (G)   No member of the Auxiliary Police Force shall engage in any activity
thereof unless he is in possession of a badge and identification card provided
by the city and is clothed in the uniform of the Auxiliary Police Force
approved by the Chief of Police, unless he is engaged in an activity in which
the disclosure of his membership in the Auxiliary Police Force would be
detrimental thereto and when such nonuniformed activity is specifically
authorized by the Chief of Police.
   (H)   Upon the failure of any member of the Auxiliary Police Force to comply
with any of the provisions hereof or of any order or direction of the Chief of
Police or any member of the Police Department to which the member of the
Auxiliary Police Force is responsible pursuant to the terms hereof, the City
Commission may either suspend or terminate the membership of that member in the
Auxiliary Police Force after providing the member with an opportunity for a
hearing in regard thereto.
   (I)   The members of the Auxiliary Police Force are hereby declared to be
agents of the city when they are acting within the course and scope of such
membership and pursuant to the rules and regulations of the city and the
Auxiliary Police Force. As such, they shall have all of the rights, privileges,
and immunities thereof. However, such members are not employees of the city but
rather are gratuitous volunteers who are not entitled to any compensation or
other monetary benefits or remuneration for their time, services, or expenses,
unless specifically authorized and approved by the City Commission.
(Ord. 2-5-84, passed - -84)
§ 35.19 POLICE DEPARTMENT RULES AND REGULATIONS.
   The Taylor Mill Police Department Rules and Regulations originally prepared
by the Northern Kentucky Area Development District in 1979 and revised in 1985
with assistance from the Government Services Institute of NKU, and any
subsequent amendments thereto which are adopted by the city by ordinance, are
made a part hereof by reference, and are made a part of the permanent records
of the city and are adopted as the official police rules and regulations of the
city.
§ 35.20 EMPLOYMENT; TRAINING COSTS.
   No applicant for employment as a police officer with the city who has not
successfully completed the basic training course described in KRS 15.440, shall
be employed without a written agreement signed by the applicant that, in the
event of any subsequent termination of employment as a police officer within
three (3) years, the applicant shall reimburse the city for all costs and
expenses incurred by the city for the applicant's participation in the basic
training course, including, without limitation, all salary and benefits paid to
or for the applicant. The following schedule of reimbursement shall apply:
   (A)   Termination within one (1) year of employment         100% of costs
   (B)   Termination between one (1) and two (2) years of
employment         75% of costs
   (C)   Termination between two (2) and three (3) years of
employment         50% of costs
(Ord. 10-23-91, passed 10-23-91)
§ 35.21 CONDITIONS FOR EMPLOYMENT OF UNTRAINED APPLICANTS AS POLICE OFFICERS.
   In addition to any other rules, regulations, policies and other conditions
of employment as a police officer of the city established by any other
ordinances and municipal orders of the City Commission, an applicant for
employment as a police officer of the City who has not graduated from the
Department of Criminal Justice Training or some other equivalent training
approved by the Kentucky Law Enforcement Commission and the Chief of the Taylor
Mill Police Department; shall also comply with the following requirements; and
no such applicant shall be employed as a police officer of the City without
complying with those requirements:
   (A)   Enter into an employment contract like or similar to the one attached
hereto and incorporated herein by reference.
   (B)   Successfully complete and graduate from the Department of Criminal
Justice Training, or other training approved by both the Kentucky Law
Enforcement Commission and the Chief of the Taylor Mill Police Department
within six months after conditional employment by the city.
(Ord. 343(04-10-2019), passed 4-10-19)
FIRE DEPARTMENT
§ 35.30 ESTABLISHMENT; FUNCTIONS.
   Subject to the legislative, executive, and administrative authority of the
City Commission, all other laws and regulations of any other governmental
agency having jurisdiction, and the budget of the city, the function of the
Fire Department shall be to provide the following services to all persons and
property within the city through contracts with the Taylor Mill Volunteer Fire
Department as authorized by the City Commission:
   (A)   Protection against fire and other natural hazards;
   (B)   Emergency medical services;
   (C)   Transportation of persons who are sick, injured, or otherwise
physically or medically incapacitated to a hospital or other location for
medical treatment or other health-care services;
   (D)   The administrative enforcement of all ordinances, orders, regulations,
and other laws in regard to the physical safety of persons and property within
the city from the hazards of medical illness or accidental physical injury
enacted by the city or by any other governmental agency with the city having
authority for the enforcement thereof.
(Ord. 1-1-86, passed 1- -86)
OTHER ADMINISTRATIVE DEPARTMENTS
§ 35.40 FINANCE DEPARTMENT.
   Subject to the legislative, executive, and administrative authority of the
City Commission and all other laws and regulations of any other governmental
agency having jurisdiction, and the budget of the city therefor, the function
of the Department of Finance established hereby shall be to provide the
following:
   (A)   The identification and analysis of all sources of revenue available to
the city; and the preparation of all ordinances, applications, contracts, or
other documents necessary therefor; and
   (B)   The development and maintenance of all accounting and financial
procedures and records which are either required by law or necessary for the
responsible fiscal operation and administration of the city, including but not
limited to the development and implementation of an annual budget therefor.
(Ord. 1-1-86, passed 1- -86)
§ 35.41 LAND USE PLANNING AND ZONING DEPARTMENT.
   Subject to the legislative, executive, and administrative authority of the
City Commission, all other laws and regulations of any other governmental
agency having jurisdiction, and the budget of the city therefor, the function
of the Land Use Planning and Zoning Department shall be to provide for:
   (A)   The preparation of a plan for the development and use of all land
within the city consistent with the requirements of all laws in regard thereto;
and the amendment thereof from time to time according to law, as the health,
benefit, and welfare of the citizens and residents of the city may require;
   (B)   The coordination of all agencies, offices, departments, and
commissions of the city and other governmental agencies with the activities,
goals, and objectives of the owners of land within the city in order to promote
and accomplish the development and use of such land according to the plan
described in division (A); and
   (C)   Subject to the authority of the City Commission, to administer all
ordinances, orders, regulations, and other laws in regard to the development
and use of land within the city and the construction and maintenance of
buildings and other structures thereon enacted by the city or any other
authorized governmental agency.
(Ord. 1-1-86, passed 1- -86)
§ 35.42 OFFICE ADMINISTRATION DEPARTMENT.
   Subject to the legislative, executive, and administrative authority of the
City Commission, all other laws and regulations of any other governmental
agency having jurisdiction, and the budget of the city therefor, the function
of the Office Administration Department shall be to provide the following:
   (A)   The maintenance and safekeeping of the permanent records of the city
and, in conjunction with this, to perform the duties of "Official Custodian" or
"Custodian" pursuant to Chapter 34 through the office of City Clerk/Tax
Collector;
   (B)   The clerical and secretarial services required by the City Commission
or other departments of the city for which no funds for such services have been
separately budgeted; and
   (C)   The civil administration and enforcement of all ordinances, orders,
and regulations of the city, the administration and enforcement of which are
not included in the function of any other department of the city pursuant to
the provisions hereof.
(Ord. 1-1-86, passed 1- -86)
Cross-reference:
   City Administrative Officer, §
31.38
§ 35.43 PARK AND RECREATION DEPARTMENT.
   (A)   Park and Recreation Department. Subject to the legislative, executive,
and administrative authority of the City Commission, all other laws and
regulations of any other governmental agency having jurisdiction, and the
budget of the city therefor, the function of the Parks and Recreation
Department shall be to provide public parks, playgrounds, recreational
programs, projects, and activities to the citizens and residents of the city
through the Park Board established by division (B) below. (Ord. 1-1-86, passed
1- -86)
   (B)   Park Board.
      (1)   Pursuant to the authority of KRS 97.550, there is hereby
established a Park Board to be known as the Taylor Mill Park Board consisting
of five members who shall each be at least 21 years of age and a resident of
the city for at least one year prior to the date of the appointment and who
shall each subscribe to the oath required by KRS 97.560.
      (2)   The terms of office of the members of the Park Board shall be for
two years and until their successors are appointed and qualified except that
three members of the first Board appointed hereby shall be appointed for terms
of only one year. The members of the Board shall not receive any salary for
their services.
      (3)   Pursuant to KRS 97.550, the Park Board shall be a corporation with
perpetual succession and may, in its corporate name, contract and be contracted
with, sue and be sued, have and use a corporate seal and alter and renew it at
pleasure.
      (4)   The members of the Park Board shall meet annually and choose a
President and a Secretary from among the members, each to serve for a term of
one year. The duties of such officers shall be the usual duties incumbent upon
such an office and such other duties as the Board prescribes. (KRS 97.570)
      (5)   The Park Board shall have responsibility for the care, management,
and control of all parks and playgrounds within the limits of the city, shall
lay out and improve them with walks, drives, roads, and trees, provide
appliances and equipment for playgrounds, and provide for the proper lighting
of the parks and playgrounds. (KRS 97.580)
      (6)   The Park Board shall keep a set of books showing the receipts and
expenditures of the Board. The books shall, at all times, be subject to
examination by the City Commission, either by themselves or by a certified
public accountant. The Park Board shall, each January, transmit to the City
Commission a full and detailed report and statement of the acts of the Board
for the preceding year, with a complete and itemized account of all receipts
and disbursements of money, and an itemized estimate of the money needed for
park and playground purposes. (KRS 97.600)
(Ord. 3-10-79, passed 10-11-79; Ord. 1-3-82, passed 3- -82)
§ 35.44 PUBLIC UTILITIES DEPARTMENT.
   Subject to the legislative, executive, and administrative authority of the
City Commission, all other laws and regulations of any other governmental
agency having jurisdiction, and the budget of the city therefor, the function
of the Public Utilities Department shall be to provide water distribution and
sewage collection services through the Taylor Mill Utilities Commission and the
Winston Park Water Commission established by previous ordinances of the city,
which shall continue to exist according to the provisions of such ordinances
with all of the authority, responsibility, and duties described therein.
(Ord. 1-1-86, passed 1- -86)
§ 35.45 PUBLIC WORKS DEPARTMENT.
   Subject to the legislative, executive, and administrative authority of the
City Commission, all other laws and regulations of any other governmental
agency having jurisdiction, and the budget of the city therefor, the function
of the Department of Public Works shall be to provide for the maintenance and
repair of all land, property, buildings, and equipment owned or used by the
city and such public roads, easements, and ways within the city as have been
accepted for maintenance by the city.
(Ord. 1-1-86, passed 1- -86; Am. Ord. 110(05-14-97), passed 5-14-97)

§ 37.01 ADOPTION BY REFERENCE.
   (A)   The city hereby adopts personnel policies as prepared by the Northern
Kentucky Area Development District, by reference as if fully suet out herein. A
copy of the policies are on file in the office of the City Clerk/Tax Collector.
   (B)   A schedule of personnel policy amendments is set out in
T.S.O. VIII.
(Ord. 37(4-22-94), passed 4-22-92; Am. Ord. 136(6-17-98), passed 6-17-98)
§ 37.02 PARTICIPATION IN RETIREMENT SYSTEM AUTHORIZED.
   (A)   The city is hereby authorized and directed to participate in the
County Employee Retirement System of Kentucky with hazardous duty coverage for
all eligible members of the police and fire departments. All eligible full time
officers and employees of the city are hereby authorized and directed to comply
with the statutory requirements of the County Employees Retirement System of
Kentucky.
   (B)   All employees of the city, whose duties require an average of one
hundred hours during each working month shall be considered as "regular full
time" employees for the purposes of the County Employee Retirement System,
except those other persons who are employed as "temporary," "part time" and
"seasonal" workers, as defined in KRS 78.510 (21) of the County Employee
Retirement Laws.
(Ord. 24(7-10-91), passed 7-10-91; Am. Ord. 25(8-14-91), passed 8-14-91)
CHAPTER 38: AFFIRMATIVE ACTION PLAN
Section
   
38.01   Statement of policy
   
38.02   Dissemination of policy
   
38.03   Personnel actions
   
38.04   Workforce utilization
   
38.05   Responsibility for implementation
   
38.06   Evaluation and reports
§ 38.01 STATEMENT OF POLICY.
   The affirmative action policy of the city is to promote equal employment
opportunity; to prohibit discrimination in employment on account of race,
color, religion, national origin, sex, age, or disability status; and to bring
about a fair representation and utilization of females and minorities on all
levels of city employment.
('78 Code, 220.1, § I) (Res. 2-10-77, passed 10-13-77)
§ 38.02 DISSEMINATION OF POLICY.
   The city will advise all employees as well as applicants for employment of
this policy and will post it in a conspicuous place. The city will make known
to the public that employment opportunities are available on the basis of
individual ability and will encourage all persons who are employed by the city
to strive for advancement on that basis.
('78 Code, 220.1, § II) (Res. 2-10-77, passed 10-13-77)
§ 38.03 PERSONNEL ACTIONS.
   The city will actively recruit qualified or qualifiable persons among
females and minorities on a nondiscriminatory basis for all available job
openings at every level. Further, the city will ensure every employee equal
treatment in respect to terms and conditions of employment, job assignments,
compensation, access to training, and promotions.
('78 Code, 220.1, § III) (Res. 2-10-77, passed 10-13-77)
§ 38.04 WORKFORCE UTILIZATION.
   The city will analyze the utilization of females and minorities in its
workforce and compare it with the utilization by all employers in the county
according to the latest official census. The goal of the city is to bring about
comparable utilization in all categories within the next five years, and then
to maintain such comparable utilization.
('78 Code, 220.1, § IV) (Res. 2-10-77, passed 10-13-77)
§ 38.05 RESPONSIBILITY FOR IMPLEMENTATION.
   Under the general supervision of the City Commission, the authorized city
official shall be responsible for implementation of this chapter, including
maintenance of the workforce analysis and job roster and the hearing of
complaints of discrimination by any employees or prospective employees of the
city. Final appeals will be heard by the City Commission.
('78 Code, 220.1, § V) (Res. 2-10-77, passed 10-13-77)
§ 38.06 EVALUATION AND REPORTS.
   The person given responsibility for implementation of this chapter shall
examine its operation periodically and report the progress being made, together
with recommendations for improvements in the plan, to the City Commission at
least once every year.
('78 Code, 220.1, § VI) (Res. 2-10-77, passed 10-13-77)
