GARBAGE COLLECTION ASSESSMENT
§ 50.01 DEFINITION.
   For the purpose of this subchapter the following definition shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   "ANYBODY." Any individual human being, or any combination thereof in the
form of a corporation, partnership, joint venture, unincorporated association
or otherwise.
   "NOBODY." No individual human being, or any combination thereof in the form
of a corporation, partnership, joint venture, unincorporated association or
otherwise.
   "UNIT." A family unit. A one-family dwelling shall constitute one "UNIT."
Each apartment in an apartment building shall be a separate "UNIT."
('78 Code, 810.2, § II; Am. Ord. 45(9-9-92), passed 9-9-92)
§ 50.02 ASSESSMENT ESTABLISHED; USE OF SERVICE REQUIRED.
   (A)   There is hereby imposed an annual waste collection assessment upon
each parcel of real estate within the corporate limits of the city. The fees
and assessments herein set forth shall be in addition to property taxes or any
license or occupational taxes imposed by any other ordinance of the city. ('78
Code, 810.2, §§ II, IV) (Ord. 1-7-73, passed - - )
   (B)   All residents and businesses are required to utilize the city's
garbage collection service.
§ 50.03 RATE OF ASSESSMENT.
   The rate of said assessment shall be two hundred and fifty five ($255)
dollars per year for each single-family residential structure within the city,
which shall be due and payable simultaneously with the ad valorem taxes of the
city.
('78 Code, 810.2, § III) (Ord. 1-7-73, passed - - ; Am. Ord. 4-4-80, passed 4-
10-80; Am. Ord. 1-9-86, passed - -; Am. Ord. 2-6-87, passed 7-9-87; Am. Ord. 9
(9-26-90), passed 9-26-90; Am. Ord. 42(8-26-92), passed 8-26-92; Am. Ord. 123
(9-10-97), passed 9-10-97; Am. Ord. 198(6-11-03), passed 6-11-03; Am. Ord. 214
(7-14-04), passed 7-14-04; Am. Ord. 229(10-12-05), passed 10-12-05; Am. Ord.
240(11-8-06), passed 11-8-06; Am. Ord. 244(6-27-07), passed 6-27-07; Am. Ord.
285(10-26-12), passed 10-26-12; Am. Ord. 303(11-28-2014), passed 11-28-14; Am.
Ord. 310(11-19-2015), passed 11-19-15; Am. Ord. 328(11-8-2017), passed 11-8-17;
Am. Ord. 337(10-10-18), passed 10-10-18; Am. Ord. 363(09-09-2020), passed 9-9-
20; Am. Ord. 372(09-08-2021), passed 9-8-21; Am. Ord. 382(09-28-2022), passed
9-28-22; Am. Ord. 391(09-28-2023), passed 9-28-23; Am. Ord. 401(09-11-2024),
passed 9-11-24)
§ 50.04 BILLING AND DUTY TO PAY.
   The assessment shall be paid in the manner prescribed by the City Clerk/Tax
Collector upon the bill provided therefore. The bill shall be mailed to the
address of the real estate or such other address as is indicated by the owner
on forms provided by the City Clerk/Tax Collector. Any person who has any
interest in any parcel of real estate in the city shall be totally and
severally liable for the waste collection assessment.
('78 Code, 810.2, § VI) Penalty, see §
50.99
§ 50.05 LIEN FOR NONPAYMENT.
   Upon any nonpayment of any waste collection assessment, the city shall have
a lien upon the real estate to secure the payment of the assessment.
('78 Code, 810.2, § VII) (Ord. 1-7-73, passed - - )
§ 50.06 LOCATION OF CONTAINERS.
   Nobody shall cause, promote, permit, aid, assist, allow, encourage or engage
in either:
   (A)   The location of any garbage can or any other container for solid waste
material anywhere in the front yard of any lot or parcel of real estate in the
city to which the city provides garbage or other waste collection services at
any time other than the twenty four (24) hour period between 4:00 P.M. on the
day before any day scheduled for the collection of garbage or other solid waste
material and 12:00 P.M. on the day scheduled for collection; or
   (B)   The location of any garbage can or any other container for solid waste
material anywhere in the side yard of any lot or parcel of real estate to which
the city provides any solid waste collection services unless the containers are
concealed from the view of anybody within the right-of-way of any public street
upon which the lot or parcel of real estate abuts.
(Ord. 45(9-9-92), passed 9-9-92)
§ 50.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Whoever fails to pay a waste collection assessment when liable
therefor as set forth in §
50.04 shall be fined no less than $10 nor more than $500 and the costs of
prosecution.
('78 Code, 810.2, § VII) (Ord. 7-7-73, passed )
   (B)   Each violation and every other failure to comply with the provisions
of §
50.06 shall be a misdemeanor. Each day of the continuation shall be a separate
and distinct offense for which:
      (1)   Anybody convicted in a court of competent jurisdiction shall be
sentenced to pay a criminal fine not to exceed that set forth in KRS 532.090
(1), and
      (2)   The offender shall be subject to a civil penalty of one hundred
($100.00) dollars for each offense, which shall be recovered by the city in a
civil action in the nature of debt if not paid by the offender within thirty
(30) days after citation.
(Ord. 45 (9-9-92), passed 9-9-92)
CHAPTER 51: SEWERS

General Provisions

GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 51.01 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this chapter the following definitions shall apply unless
the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   "PRIVATE SEWAGE DISPOSAL SYSTEM." Any system of pipes, drains, and conduits
owned, operated, and maintained by any person other than the city for the
purpose of collection and distribution of liquid waste material from real
estate located within the city.
   "SEWER SYSTEM." That system of pipes, drains, and conduits owned, operated,
or maintained by the city for the collection and distribution of liquid waste
material from real estate located within the city.
   "SEWER USER." Any person who owns real estate within or without the city,
upon which is located a private sewage disposal system which is connected
directly to the city sewer system.
   "SEWERABLE PROPERTY." Any parcel of real estate within the city which abuts
upon any public or private right-of-way or easement at a point where there is
located therein any portion of the city sewer system.
   "UNIT." Each portion of a structure which is occupied or intended to be
occupied by a person or his family, business, or any other association or
organization, whether incorporated or unincorporated, which is exclusively
separate and apart from the remaining portions of the structure, whether the
portion is used for residential, commercial, or industrial purposes.
(Ord. 1-7-80, passed 7-10-80)
§ 51.02 CONNECTION TO SYSTEM, PAYMENT OF FEES REQUIRED.
   (A)   No person shall cause or permit any sewerable property on which there
is located a private sewage disposal system to be used for any purpose unless
the private sewage disposal system thereon is connected directly to the city
sewage disposal system pursuant to the regulations of the city and until the
fees established by the terms hereof for the use of the sewage disposal system
have been paid.
   (B)   All private sewage disposal systems located on formerly non- sewerable
property shall be connected to the city sewer system within 30 days of the
property's becoming sewerable property as a result of the expansion of the city
sewer system. All owners of sewerable property shall, within 30 days after
connection into the sewer system, destroy or cause to be destroyed any
privately-owned privy, cesspool, or septic tank and shall cause the ground
where such privy, cesspool, or septic tank is located to be covered with lime
or other germ- destroying chemical.
(Ord. 1-7-80, passed 7-10-80) Penalty, see §
51.99
§ 51.03 COMPLIANCE WITH REGULATIONS REQUIRED.
   (A)   The Utility Commission is hereby authorized to promulgate regulations
governing connection to and use of the city sewer system consistent with this
and any other relevant ordinances of this city, and all persons shall abide by
such regulations.
   (B)   All sewer users shall abide by the rules and regulations promulgated
by Sanitation District No. 1 of Campbell and Kenton Counties, for its customers
and shall pay all fees charged by the District for sewage treatment. All
private sewage disposal systems must comply with all state and local codes.
(Ord. 1-7-80, passed 7-10-80) Penalty, see §
51.99
§ 51.04 CONNECTION TO WATER SUPPLY.
   Any unit serviced by both the city sewer system and the city water system
shall not be connected to any other source of water supply, including a water
cistern.
(Ord. 1-7-80, passed 7-10-80) Penalty, see §
51.99
§ 51.05 PERMITTING WATER TO EMPTY INTO SEWER SYSTEM.
   No sewer user shall permit water from any source including surface
rainwater, other than from the principal source of water supply of the
particular unit, to empty into a sewage collection system connected to the city
sewer system.
(Ord. 1-7-80, passed 7-10-80) Penalty, see §
51.99
CLASSIFICATION OF USERS; FEES
§ 51.15 CLASSIFICATION OF SEWER USERS ESTABLISHED.
   The following types of sewer users are established pursuant to KRS 96.910 et
seq.:
   (A)   Type I. Any sewer user not described as a Type II, Type III, or Type
IV sewer user as herein defined.
   (B)   Type II. A sewer user whose property is connected to an internal
public collector line of at least eight inches in diameter which was
constructed as part of a subdivision development at no cost to the city but
which system drains into a sewer line constructed by the city.
   (C)   Type III. A sewer user whose property is connected to an internal
public collector line of at least eight inches in diameter which was
constructed as part of a subdivision development at no cost to the city, which
system does not drain into any portion of a sewer line which was constructed by
the city. Notwithstanding any of the foregoing classifications, all owners of
homes in the Mill Valley Subdivision shall be considered Type III customers in
consideration of the developer's construction of sewer lines for the city.
   (D)   Type IV. A sewer user whose property is located within the old
corporate limits of the former City of Winston Park and which is connected to
that former city's system.
   (E)   Type V. A sewer user whose property is connected to the sanitary sewer
line along Grand Avenue, Winona Drive, Fairview Avenue, and Reidlin Road which
was constructed by the city with a federal grant.
(Ord. 1-7-80, passed 7-10-80; Am. Ord. 6-8-88, passed 8-18-88)
§ 51.16 CONNECTION CHARGES.
   The following charges are established for connection to the city sewer
system:
   (A)   Type I and Type V sewer users shall pay a one-time tapping fee of $400
per connection to the sewer system, the amount to be paid at the time
application for connection is made. The sewer user shall not be permitted to
connect to the system until the fee is paid.
   (B)   Type II, Type III, and Type IV sewer users shall pay a one- time
tapping fee of $200 per connection to be paid upon connection of the
subdivision's internal public collector system to the city sewer system or upon
connection of the sewer user's private sewage disposal system to the city sewer
system, whichever last occurs. If the fee is to be paid upon connection to the
sewer system in accordance with the above, then the fee shall be paid before
connection is permitted. If the fee is to be paid upon connection of the
subdivision internal public collector system to the city sewer system, then the
fee shall be paid by all sewer users of the subdivision system within 30 days
of the connection.
   (C)   Notwithstanding the provisions of divisions (A) and (B) above, all
sewer users shall pay a one-time tapping fee of $500 per connection instead of
the fee provided for in (A) or (B) of this section, if the city must provide a
connection sleeve to an existing sewer line in order to accommodate the
connection. This fee must be paid at the time the request for connection is
made.
(Ord. 1-7-80, passed 7-10-80; Am. Ord. 1-7-85, passed 9-12-85; Am. Ord. 6-8-88,
passed 8-18-88)
§ 51.17 DEBT SERVICE CHARGES.
   (A)   In addition to the charges set out in §
51.16, there shall be the following debt service charge to be paid by Type I
and II sewer users.
      (1)   Type I. A charge of $9.00 per month per unit for each and every
month or portion thereof the unit is connected with the city sewer system.
      (2)   Type II. A charge of $4.50 per month per unit for each and every
month or portion thereof the unit is connected with the city sewer system.
   (B)   The charges set out in division (A) above shall be eliminated by
action of the City Commission, upon a determination by the Utility Commission
that all the debt incurred in the construction of the sewer system has been
recovered.
(Ord. 1-7-80, passed 7-10-80)
§ 51.18 BASIC SEWER CHARGE.
   In addition to the charges set out in §§
51.16 and
51.17, every sewer user shall pay a basic sewer charge of $7.50 per calendar
quarter per unit for each and every calendar quarter or portion thereof such
unit is connected with the city sewer system. When the fund created by this
charge reaches $500,000, this basic charge will be eliminated until such fund
is reduced to $300,000, at which time the basic charge will be re-established.
(Ord. 1-7-80, passed 7-10-80; Am. Ord. 1-4-83, passed 5-26-83)
§ 51.19 DUE DATE; PENALTY FOR DELINQUENCY.
   (A)   All charges set out in §§
51.17 and
51.18 are to be paid within 30 days of the end of the calendar quarter in which
the connection exists.
   (B)   All fees and charges unpaid when due, including the fees described in
§
51.16, shall have added thereto a penalty of 10%, plus interest at the rate of
8% per annum, until paid.
(Ord. 1-7-80, passed 7-10-80) Penalty, see §
51.99
§ 51.20 LIABILITY FOR FEES FOR PRIVATE SYSTEM CONNECTED TO SEWER SYSTEM.
   The owners of real estate located within the city upon which is located a
private sewage disposal system which is connected to the city sewage disposal
system shall be jointly and severally liable for the fees established pursuant
to the terms hereof for the use of the sewage disposal system, plus all
penalties and interest in regard thereto and the costs of the collection
thereof, including court costs and attorney fees. In order to secure the
payment of such sums, the city shall have a lien upon the real estate.
(Ord. 1-7-80, passed 7-10-80) Penalty, see §
51.99
§ 51.21 FEES TO BE PAID TO SANITATION DISTRICT.
   All fees, penalties, and interest established pursuant to the terms of this
chapter shall be paid to the city or to Sanitation District No. 1 of Campbell
and Kenton Counties as the collecting agent for the city.
(Ord. 1-7-80, passed 7-10-80)
§ 51.22 DISPOSITION OF FUNDS.
   (A)   All fees, penalties, and interest received by the city, pursuant to §
51.18 shall be deposited in a special fund designated as the Taylor Mill Sewer
System Maintenance Fund, and shall be used only for the maintenance, repair,
replacement, and expansion of the city sewer system.
   (B)   All fees, penalties, and interest received by the city pursuant to §§
51.16 and
51.17 shall be deposited in a special fund designated as the Taylor Mill Sewer
System Debt Retirement Fund, and shall be used only for the construction and
retirement of debt of the city sewer system.
(Ord. 1-7-80, passed 7-10-80)
§ 51.99 PENALTY.
   Any person who violates any of the terms or provisions of this chapter shall
be, upon conviction, guilty of a misdemeanor and be fined not less than $10 nor
more than $500 or imprisoned for not more than 60 days or both. Each day's
violation shall be a separate offense.
(Ord. 1-7-80, passed 7-10-80)
CHAPTER 52: ELECTRIC UTILITY FRANCHISE FEE
Section
   
52.01   Payment of fee for electricity franchise required; amount
§ 52.01 PAYMENT OF FEE FOR ELECTRICITY FRANCHISE REQUIRED; AMOUNT.
   Any person who has a franchise with the city for the use of the public ways
and grounds of the city for the transmission and distribution of electricity
shall pay to the city within 90 days of the receipt thereof, a fee of 3% of the
gross receipts collected by such person from customers from the sale of
electricity within the corporate limits of the city.
(Ord. 2-7-81, passed 8-13-81)

WINSTON PARK WATER COMMISSION
§ 53.01 WINSTON WATER PARK WATER COMMISSION ESTABLISHED.
   There is hereby established a board of three (3) commissioners to be known
as the Winston Park Water Commission.
(T.M. Ord. 9-1-73, passed 1-11-73; T.M. Code 1974, § 111.01; Am. Ord. 3-3-89,
passed 3-9-89)
§ 53.02 DUTIES.
   The duties of the water commission shall be to operate, manage, and maintain
the existing water distribution system in the section of the city which lies
north of Banklick Creek. The duties shall be exercised in accordance with the
provisions of KRS Chapter 106.
(T.M. Ord. 9-1-73, passed 1-11-73; T.M. Code 1974, § 111.03; Am. Ord. 3-3-89,
passed 3-9-89)
§ 53.03 TERMS.
   The terms of office of the water commissioners shall be for a period of
three (3) years, and which shall be staggered so that no more than one
commissioner shall be appointed in any year.
(T.M. Ord. 9-1-73, passed 1-11-73; T.M. Code 1974, § 111.05; Am. Ord. 3-3-89;
passed 3-9-89)
§ 53.04 COMPENSATION.
   No compensation shall be paid to any person for serving as a member of the
water commission.
(T.M. Ord. 9-1-73, passed 1-11-73; T.M. Code 1974, § 111.07; Am. Ord. 3-3-89,
passed 3-9-89)
§ 53.05 AUTHORITY.
   The board of commissioners may enter into such contracts and hire such
personnel as are necessary to carry out the provisions of this chapter, and
shall conduct all business under the name of the Winston Park Water Commission.
(T.M. Ord. 9-1-73, passed 1-11-73, T.M. Code 1974, § 111.09; Am. Ord. 3-3-89,
passed 3-9-89)
§ 53.06 LIABILITY: PAYMENT OF DEBTS.
   The board of commissioners shall be responsible for the payment of the debts
of the commission only to the extent that there are assets of the commission
available for such purposes. In no event should any member of the Winston Park
Water Commission be personally liable for the payment of any obligation of the
commission.
(T.M. Ord. 9-1-73, passed 1-11-73; T.M. Code 1974, § 111.11; Am. Ord. 3-3-89,
passed 3-9-89)
REGULATIONS
§ 53.15 INSTALLATION OF METERS.
   The water commission shall install water meters in every house in the city
which lies north of Banklick Creek, and which fronts on any street wherein
water mains have been installed.
(W.P. Ord. 9-1933, passed 10-2-33; T.M. Code 1974, § 111.13; Am. Ord. 3-3-89,
passed 3-9-89)
§ 53.16 CHARGE FOR INSTALLATION.
   (A)   A flat charge of twenty-five ($25.00) dollars shall be made for the
installation of a meter and connections thereto for any new house. The charge
is payable before the building permit is granted.
   (B)   The installation of pipes for water service in any building in the
city which lies north of Banklick Creek, shall be made in such a manner that
the meter can be installed, without altering or changing any of the pipes, by
leaving a space of sufficient width for the insertion of the meter. This space,
however, may be filled by a short piece of pipe in such a manner as to make the
short piece of pipe easily removable. The owner of any building or the plumber
performing the work shall, in addition to the flat charge of twenty-five
($25.00) dollars set out above, deposit with the clerk of the city an
additional sum of twenty-five ($25.00) dollars. In the event any installation
of pipes for water service is made without providing a space for the
installation of the meter, the city shall hire a plumber to make whatever
changes are necessary and pay the expense out of the deposit of twenty-five
($25.00) dollars. In the event the installation is properly made, the twenty-
five ($25.00) dollars is to be returned to the party making the deposit.
(W.P. Ord. 2-1950, § 1, passed 4-10-50; T.M. Code 1974, § 111.15; Am. Ord. 3-3-
89; passed 3-9-89)
§ 53.17 COLLECTION OF AUTHORIZED REVENUE; USE.
   The water commission is hereby authorized to collect all water rents and
other charges and to keep the revenue in a separate fund to be known as the
water fund. The revenue derived from water rents and other charges shall be
used only for the purchase of water and water meters and for other necessary
expenses of operating the water system.
(W.P. Ord. 9-1933, § 4, passed 10-2-33; T.M. Code 1974, § 111.17; Am. Ord. 3-3-
89, passed 3-9-89)
§ 53.18 WATER RATES.
   The water commission shall charge a rate of fifteen dollars ($15.00) per
quarter year for the first one thousand (1,000) cubic feet used by the
occupants of each house or apartment, and a further charge of one dollar and
fifty cents ($1.50) per one hundred cubic feet for all water consumed by the
occupants of each house or apartment over and above one thousand (1,000) cubic
feet per quarter year.
(W.P. Ord. 9-1952, § 1, passed 12-3-52; T.M. Code 1974, § 111.19; Am. Ord. 3-3-
89, passed 3-9-89)
§ 53.19 DELINQUENT PAYMENTS; TERMINATION OF WATER SERVICE.
   (A)   The charges for water are payable at the end of each quarter and if
not paid within thirty (30) days after the end of each quarter, a penalty of
ten percent (10%) of the amount of the bill shall be added and the bill placed
in the hands of the police for collection.
   (B)   In the event the amount of the bill plus the ten percent (10%) penalty
is not paid to the police within five (5) days after being notified by the
police that the bill is delinquent, the water commission shall shut off the
water supply. An additional charge of one ($1.00) dollar shall be made when the
water is turned back on.
   (C)   If owing to unemployment or financial reverses any person is unable to
pay the water bill when due, the city council of the city may, if they deem
proper, exempt the person from the penalty herein provided and permit the
person to continue to use water, but the charges will not be remitted.
(W.P. Ord. 9-1952, § 1, passed 12-3-52; T.M. Code 19-4, § 111.21; Am. Ord. 3-3-
89, passed 3-9-89)
§ 53.20 APPLICATION FOR SERVICE.
   Any person, firm, or corporation which lies in the section of the city north
of Banklick Creek desiring to become a consumer of water shall make application
to the Clerk of the city. The application shall be accompanied by a cash
deposit of five ($5.00) dollars as a guarantee that the applicant shall pay for
the water consumed. The five ($5.00) dollar deposit shall be refunded to the
applicant when he ceases to be a consumer of water in the aforementioned area,
providing that all previous water bills have been paid in full.
(W.P. Ord. 9-1952, § 1, passed 12-2-52; T.M. Code 1974, § 111.23; Am. Ord. 3-3-
89, passed 3-9-89)
§ 53.21 RESPONSIBILITY FOR REPAIR.
   (A)   In cases of needed repair to water lines, if any trouble occurs on the
water line from the building to the cut-off valve it is the responsibility of
the property owner. If any trouble occurs in the cut-off valve or in the main
water line it is the responsibility of the city.
(W.P. Ord. 2-1964, passed 3-4-64; T.M. Code 1974, § 111.25; Am. Ord. 3-3-89,
passed 3-9-89)
   (B)   All water meters and cut-off valves shall be maintained by the
customer or the owner of the property or real estate serviced thereby, in a
condition which is visible and accessible to the city, and the Winston Park
Water Commission, and the officers, agents, servants and employees thereof.
(Ord. 3-3-89, passed 3-9-89)
§ 53.22 WATER CUT-OFF VALVES.
   (A)   All water cut-off valves shall be placed at the curb of the street in
front of the building to be supplied with water unless the building inspector
orders the cut-off valve placed at some other secure and convenient place.
Building inspector orders with respect to the placement of water cut-off valves
must be in writing.
   (B)   All water cut-off valves shall be placed in cast iron chambers.
(W.P. Ord. 2-1961, § 1, passed 1-3-61; T.M. Code 1974, § 111.27; Am. Ord. 3-3-
89, passed 3-9-89)
§ 53.23 TAMPERING WITH WATER SUPPLY PROHIBITED.
   It shall be unlawful for any person, firm, or corporation to tamper with any
water meter, shut-off valve or box, or to turn off or on the water supply. This
section shall not apply to a duly authorized agent or employee of the water
department in the performance of his duties.
(W.P. Ord. 17-1934, § 2, passed 7-2-34; T.M. Code 1974, § 82.03; Am. Ord. 3-3-
89, passed 3-9-89)
§ 53.24 USE OF CLASS 52 DUCTILE IRON PIPE FOR ADDITIONS TO SYSTEM.
   Nobody shall cause, permit, promote, aid, assist, allow, encourage or engage
in the use of any pipe other than Class 52 Ductile Iron Pipe for connections to
or extensions of the water distribution system owned and operated by the city.
(Ord. 150(6-9-99), passed 6-9-99) Penalty, see §
53.99
MUNICIPAL WATERWORKS SYSTEM
§ 53.30 RATES AND CHARGES: CONNECTION FEES.
   The following fees and charges are hereby established for connections to and
the use of the water system and the receipt of water therefrom:
   (A)   A connection fee is hereby established for all new connections to the
water system after the effective date of this section, which shall be the total
of the following amounts, which must be paid to the city before the connection
will be installed:
      (1)   $750 for each 5/8" or 3/4" meter required for the connection.
      (2)   $1,050 for each 1" meter required for the connection.
      (3)   $150 for each pressure regulator determined by the city to be
reasonably necessary for the connection.
      (4)   110% of the total cost of the city for each connection in excess of
1", including, without limitation, the meter and all labor, materials,
equipment and fuel necessary for the connection.
   (B)   A monthly usage fee is hereby established, at the following rates, for
the amount of water provided by the water system through each connection:

   (C)   The monthly usage fees hereby established shall be computed according
to the number of gallons of water flowing through each connection to the water
system each month, according to the water meter therefore. In the event that
correct information isn't obtained by the city from a water meter for any
monthly period, regardless of the reason therefor, the meter information for
that monthly period shall be the weighted average of the information for that
meter during the generally corresponding monthly periods for the previous two
calendar years. If only one history period for the month is available it will
be used as the estimate. If a history period for the month is not available the
computer will use the most recent history period. If there is no history
available the operator must key in an estimate.
   (D)   A monthly fire hydrant protection fee is hereby established in the
amount of $1 for each connection to the system, in addition to the monthly
usage fees hereinbefore established, for the availability of a supply of water
at no additional charge from fire hydrants in the system, for the
extinguishment of uncontrolled fires on any parcel of real estate serviced by
the water system.
   (E)   Services charges for the maintenance and repair of connections to the
water system are hereby established at the following rates:
      (1)   $30 per hour, with a minimum of $30 during the period after 7:30
a.m. and before 3:30 p.m. on any day that isn't a Saturday, Sunday or a city
holiday.
      (2)   $50 per hour, with a minimum of $50 during any other time which
isn't on a city holiday.
      (3)   $100 per hour, with a minimum of $100, during any time on any city
holiday.
   (F)   A fee of $30 is hereby established for each time the supply of water
to a connection to the water system is either turned on or turned off by the
city, for any violation of this section or any ordinance of the city, or
pursuant to KRS 220.510, which shall be due and payable before the supply of
water thereto is turned back on.
   (G)   A reinstallation fee of $50 is hereby established for the
reinstallation or remediation of any water meter that has been the subject of
any tampering or any other unauthorized adjustments.
   (H)   A returned check fee of $13 is hereby established for each check
returned to the city without payment thereof.
   (I)   Nobody other than officers, agents, employees and volunteers of the
city, acting within the authority thereof, shall conspire, cause, permit,
promote, allow, aid, assist, encourage or engage in the receipt or use of any
water directly from a fire hydrant of the water system, except for the
extinguishment of uncontrolled fires, without:
      (1)   Renting a water meter from the city, for a specific number of days
at the non-refundable rate of $25 per day, payable in advance;
      (2)   Using the rented water meter to measure the amount of water
obtained from the water system through the fire hydrant thereof; and then
returning the rented water meter to the city, at the end of the period for
which it was rented; and simultaneously therewith, paying the city for the
water obtained at the rate of the city for water meters in excess of two
inches; and
      (3)   Depositing the separate sum of $500 with the city simultaneously
with the water meter rental, to secure both: (1) the return of the rented meter
to the city, at the end of the period for which it was rented, and in the same
condition that it was in when it was rented; and (2) the payment of the
aforedescribed fee of the city for the water obtained through the fire hydrant.
Upon the return of the rented water meter to the city at the end of the period
for which it was rented, and the simultaneous payment of the fees of the city
for the water obtained through the fire hydrant, the $500 security deposit
shall be returned or refunded by the city to the person who paid it; but
otherwise, the $500 security deposit shall be forfeited to the city, in
addition to any other penalties provided for the violation of this section.
   (J)   No water or services shall be provided by the water system through any
connection thereto, unless the owner(s) of the parcel of real estate serviced
thereby have, at least five business days prior to the effective date thereof,
provided the city with their written agreement, on a form provided by the city
to pay all usage fees, taxes, penalties, interest and collection costs incurred
therefor while they are the owners of that parcel of real estate, with the
monthly usage fees and the taxes thereon for any calendar month in which there
is a change in the ownership of that parcel of real estate pro-rated between
the new and old owners, on a daily average basis, for the period of the month
before and after the date of the transfer of ownership. The agreement of the
owner(s) may be terminated only through a written notice thereof, effective no
sooner than two business days after the receipt thereof by the city.
   (K)   Water system bills.
      (1)   Issuance to owners of real estate: At the end of every calendar
month, or shortly thereafter, the city shall issue a bill to the owners of each
parcel of real estate serviced by the water system, for all unpaid water system
fees related to that parcel of real estate, and the taxes thereon, which shall
be immediately due and payable, and which shall become delinquent on the next
following the 15th day of the calendar month, unless payment thereof is
received by the water system prior thereto; and, thereafter, such fees shall be
subject to a penalty of 15% thereof, plus collection costs, including, without
limitation, court costs and reasonable attorney fees.
      (2)   Alternate addresses and recipients: Upon the receipt of a written
authorization therefor from the owners of a parcel of real estate serviced by
the water system, the city shall cause the bills for the water system fees
related to that parcel of real estate to be issued to any other person or
address identified by the owners, but the owners thereof shall not be released
thereby from their obligation for the payment thereof.
      (3)   Accommodation mailing: As an accommodation only, the water system
may attempt to cause water system bills to be delivered to the addressee
thereof through the U. S. Postal Service; but the water system shall have no
responsibility for such delivery; and any failure therein shall not relieve the
owner(s) of the real estate from their responsibility and obligation for the
payment thereof.
   (L)   Termination of water service for non-payment of fees or other
violations of this section. The supply of water through a meter for which any
bill has become delinquent and remains unpaid, or which is any way related to
any violation of this section, or through which water is provided to any parcel
of real estate upon which any violation of any provision of this section has
occurred during the previous 12 months, shall be discontinued and turned off by
the water system; but only after a written notice thereof has been mailed to
the addressee of the water system bills therefor, more than ten days prior
thereto, with a description of the procedure by which the delinquency or
violation may be disputed; provided, however, that in the event that a written
notice that the delinquency or violation is disputed has been received by the
water system before the water is turned off, the water shall not be turned off
until the delinquency or violation is determined to exist, through an
administrative hearing conducted by the City Administrative Officer, which
conforms to all of the constitutional requirements of due process therefore.
   (M)   Nobody other than officers, agents, employees and volunteers of the
city, acting within the authority thereof, shall conspire, cause, permit,
promote, allow, aid, assist, encourage or engage in either:
      (1)   The receipt, possession or use of any water from the water system,
otherwise than through a meter for which the city has a written agreement to
pay the city fees and charges therefor, at the rates and times established by
the city; or
      (2)   Any tampering with or other adjustments to any water meter or other
equipment of the water system.
(Ord. 166(10-25-00), passed 10-25-00; Am. Ord. 201(8-13-03), passed 8-13-03;
Am. Ord. 204(10-8-03), passed 10-8-03)
§ 53.99 PENALTY.
   Each violation and every other failure to comply with the provisions of §§
53.24 and
53.30 shall be a misdemeanor; and each day of the continuation thereof shall be
a separate and distinct offense for which:
   (A)   Everybody convicted thereof in a court of competent jurisdiction shall
be sentenced to pay a criminal fine not to exceed the maximum amount of $500.00
as set forth in KRS 534.040(2)(a) or a term of imprisonment not to exceed the
maximum period of twelve (12) months as set forth in KRS 532.090(1), or both;
and
   (B)   The offender shall be subject to a civil penalty of $100 for each
offense, which shall be recovered by the city in a civil action in the nature
of debt if not paid by the offender within 30 days after citation for the
violation or other failure to comply with the provisions of §§
53.24 and
53.30.
(Ord. 150(6-9-99), passed 6-9-99; Am. Ord. 166(10-25-00), passed 10-25-00)

§ 70.01 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this title the following definitions shall apply unless
the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   "ANYBODY." Any human being, or any organization or combination thereof, in
the form of a corporation, partnership, joint venture, unincorporated
association, or otherwise.
   "AUTHORIZED EMERGENCY VEHICLES." Vehicles of the Fire Department or Police
Department, vehicles of the Commonwealth Attorney's office when on official
business, and ambulances on an authorized emergency run.
   "BOULEVARD." Any legally designated street at which cross traffic is
required to stop before entering or crossing such boulevard.
   "BUSINESS DISTRICT." Any portion of any street between two consecutive
intersections in which 50% or more of the frontage on either side of the street
is used for business purposes.
   "CROSSWALK." That portion of the roadway included within the extension of
the sidewalk across any intersection, and such other portions of the roadway
between two intersections, as may be legally designated as crossing places and
marked by stanchions, paint lines, or otherwise.
   "CURB." The boundary of that portion of the street used for vehicles whether
marked by curbstones or not.
   "INTERSECTION." That part of the public way embraced within the extensions
of the street lines of two or more streets which join at an angle whether or
not one such street crosses the other.
   "MOTOR VEHICLE." Any wheeled vehicle propelled by any means other than
muscular power.
   "NOBODY." No human being, or any organization or combination thereof, in the
form of a corporation, partnership, joint venture, unincorporated association,
or otherwise.
   "OFFICIAL TRAFFIC-CONTROL DEVICES." All signs, signals, warnings,
directions, markings, and devices placed or erected or maintained by authority
of the City Commission.
   "ONE-WAY STREET." A street on which vehicles are permitted to move in one
direction only.
   "OPERATOR." Every person who is in actual physical control of the guidance,
starting, and stopping of a vehicle.
   "PARK." When applied to vehicles, to leave a vehicle standing, whether
occupied or not, for a period of time longer than is necessary to receive or
discharge passengers or property.
   "PEDESTRIAN." Any person afoot.
   "PLAY STREET." Any street or portion thereof so designated by the City
Commission and reserved as a play area for children, from which any traffic is
barred, except vehicles to and from abutting properties.
   "POLICE DEPARTMENT." The Police Department or other persons or agency
authorized to perform the duties of §
70.03 or any other acts necessary to implement and enforce this traffic code.
   "PUBLIC WAY." The entire width between property lines of every way,
dedicated passway, or street set aside for public travel, except bridle paths
and foot paths.
   "REVERSE TURN." To turn a vehicle on any street in such a manner as to
proceed in the opposite direction.
   "RIGHT-OF-WAY." The privilege of the immediate and preferential use of the
street.
   "ROADWAY." That portion of any street, improved, designated, or ordinarily
used for vehicular travel.
   "SIDEWALK." That portion of the street between the curb and the property
line intended for the use of pedestrians.
   "STOP SIGN." A stop sign designed, made, installed, and maintained according
to the specifications of the Bureau of Highways of the Transportation Cabinet
of the Commonwealth of Kentucky.
   "STOPPING." As applied to vehicles, to stop a vehicle longer than is
actually necessary to receive or discharge passengers.
   "STOP SIGN." A stop sign designed, made, installed, and maintained according
to the specifications of the Bureau of Highways of the Transportation Cabinet
of the Commonwealth of Kentucky.
   "STREET." Every public way, including alleys.
   "TRAFFIC." Pedestrians, ridden or herded animals, vehicles, buses, and other
conveyances, individually or collectively, while using any street for the
purpose of travel.
   "VEHICLE." Every device in, on, or by which any person or property is or may
be transported or drawn on any street except devices moved by human power or
used exclusively on stationary rails or tracks.
(Am. Ord. 71(10-12-94), passed 10-12-94; Am. Ord. 100(10-23-96), passed 10-23-
96; Am. Ord. 109(04-23-97), passed 4-23-97; Am. Ord. 155(10-13-99), passed 10-
13-99; Am. Ord. 187(5-22-02), passed 5-22-02; Am. Ord. 193(9-25-02), passed 9-
25-02)
§ 70.02 REQUIRED OBEDIENCE TO TRAFFIC DIRECTIONS.
   (A)   It shall be unlawful for any person to fail or refuse to comply with
any lawful order, signal, or direction given by a uniformed police officer, or
to fail or refuse to comply with any of the traffic regulations of this traffic
code.
   (B)   The provisions of this traffic code shall apply to the driver of any
vehicle owned or used in the service of the United States government, this
state, county, or city, and it shall be unlawful for any such driver to violate
any of the provisions of this traffic code, except as otherwise permitted in
this traffic code or by state statute.
   (C)   Every person propelling any pushcart or riding a bicycle or an animal
on any roadway, and every person driving any animal on any roadway, and every
person driving any animal-drawn vehicle shall be subject to the provisions of
this traffic code applicable to the driver of any vehicle, except those
provisions of this traffic code which by their very nature can have no
application.
Penalty, see §
70.99
§ 70.03 POWERS AND DUTIES OF POLICE DEPARTMENT.
   It shall be the duty of the Police Department to direct all traffic in
conformance with this traffic code and to enforce the traffic regulations as
set forth in this traffic code, to make arrest for traffic violations, to
investigate accidents, and to cooperate with other officers of the city in the
administration of the traffic laws, and in developing ways and means to improve
traffic conditions.
§ 70.04 AUTHORITY FOR ENFORCEMENT.
   (A)   Authority to direct and enforce all traffic regulations of this city
in accordance with the provisions of this traffic code and to make arrests for
traffic violations is given to the Police Department, and, except in case of
emergency, it shall be unlawful for any other person to direct or attempt to
direct traffic by voice, hand, whistle, or any other signal.
   (B)   The Fire Chief shall have authority to issue emergency traffic
regulations as he deems necessary during the fighting of a fire. The Police
Department shall enforce his orders in this respect. ('78 Code, 520.5, § IV
(a))
Penalty, see §
70.99
§ 70.05 TEMPORARY REGULATIONS.
   When required for the convenience and safety of the public and to alleviate
unusual traffic problems, the City Commission, Chief of Police, or other
authorized city official shall, at his discretion, have authority to impose
such traffic regulations as he may deem necessary for temporary periods not to
exceed two weeks. If these temporary regulations are necessary for a period
longer than two weeks, the City Clerk/Tax Collector shall be notified in
writing of the extended order.
§ 70.06 AUTHORITY TO ERECT SIGNS.
   The City Commission may at any regular or special meeting designate and
determine parking and loading zones for passenger and freight vehicles,
establish traffic lanes, safety zones, and quiet zones, determine and designate
one-way streets, place and maintain traffic-control devices where it may deem
necessary to regulate traffic, and make any other rules and regulations it may
deem necessary to regulate traffic and the use of the streets.
('78 Code, 530.1, § I (a))
§ 70.07 EXEMPTIONS.
   The provisions of this traffic code regulating the movement or parking of
vehicles shall not apply to emergency vehicles while the driver thereof is
engaged in the performance of emergency duties. Nor shall such provisions apply
to persons actually engaged in repairing or otherwise improving the streets
under the authority of the City Commission, the state, or Kenton County. The
foregoing exemption shall not protect the driver of any such vehicle from the
consequences of his reckless disregard of the safety of others.
('78 Code, 520.5, § I)
§ 70.08 HANDICAPPED PARKING SIGNS.
   (A)   As used herein, the words “HANDICAPPED PARKING SIGN” mean a sign
bearing the international symbol of access adopted by Rehabilitation
International, in 1969.
   (B)   The executive authority of the city shall cause handicapped parking
signs to be installed, located and maintained at any one location on a street
abutting the residence of an applicant therefore, during the year thereafter,
while:
      (1)   The applicant is a person to whom there has been issued either an
accessible parking registration plate, pursuant to KRS 186.042, or an
accessible parking placard, pursuant to KRS 189.456; and
      (2)   The residence of the applicant has no driveway, or any other type
of motor vehicle parking area; and
      (3)   Motor vehicle parking is otherwise allowed at the location for
which a handicapped parking sign is requested.
   (C)   The installation, location and maintenance of a handicapped parking
sign, shall not relieve or exempt anybody from complying with all other
statutes and ordinances regulating motor vehicle parking at the location
thereof.
(Ord. 113(6-11-97), passed 6-11-97)
TRAFFIC-CONTROL DEVICES
§ 70.15 SIGNAL LEGENDS.
   Whenever traffic is regulated or controlled exclusively by a traffic-control
sign or signs exhibiting the words "Go," "Caution," or "Stop," or exhibiting
different colored lights for purposes of traffic control, the following colors
only shall be used, and these terms and lights shall indicate and be obeyed as
follows:
   (A)   Green alone or "Go": Vehicular traffic facing the signal may proceed
straight through or turn right or left unless a sign at such place prohibits
either such turn. However, vehicular traffic shall yield the right-of-way to
other vehicles and to pedestrians lawfully within the intersection at the time
such signal is exhibited.
   (B)   Steady yellow alone or "Caution" when shown following the green or
"Go" signal: Vehicular traffic facing a steady yellow signal is thereby warned
that the related green movement is being terminated or that a red indication
will be exhibited immediately thereafter when vehicular traffic shall not enter
the intersection. Vehicular traffic facing a steady yellow signal may enter and
clear the intersection.
   (C)   Red alone or double red or "Stop": Vehicular traffic facing the signal
shall stop before entering the nearest crosswalk at an intersection or at such
other point as may be indicated by a clearly visible line, and shall remain
standing until green or "Go" is shown alone.
   (D)   Flashing red alone: Vehicular traffic facing the signal shall stop
before entering the nearest crosswalk at an intersection or at such other point
as may be indicated by a clearly visible line, and shall not again proceed
until it can do so without danger.
   (E)   Flashing amber alone: Vehicular traffic facing the signal shall reduce
its speed and proceed cautiously across the intersection controlled by such
signal.
   (F)   "Yield Right-of-Way": Vehicular traffic facing the "Yield Right-of-
Way" sign shall bear the primary responsibility of safely entering the primary
intersecting or merging right-of-way. All traffic facing the sign shall yield
the right-of-way to all vehicles and pedestrians within such primary
intersecting or merging right-of-way. No vehicle facing a "Yield Right-of-Way"
sign shall enter the merging or intersecting right-of-way at a speed in excess
of 15 miles per hour, except that this speed limit shall not apply to vehicles
entering an expressway.
   (G)   Lane lights: When lane lights are installed over any street for the
purpose of controlling the direction of flow of traffic, vehicular traffic
shall move only in traffic lanes over which green arrows appear. However, when
flashing yellow lights appear above a lane all left turns shall be made from
that lane. Where red arrows appear above such lanes, vehicles shall not move
against them. If flashing yellow lights show above a lane, that lane shall be
used only for passing and for left turns unless a sign at such place prohibits
such turn.
Penalty, see §
70.99
Statutory reference:
   Traffic-control signals, see KRS 189.338
§ 70.16 ESTABLISHMENT AND MAINTENANCE OF TRAFFIC-CONTROL DEVICES.
   The city shall establish and maintain all official traffic-control devices
necessary within the city. All traffic-control devices, including signs, shall
be employed to indicate one particular warning or regulation, shall be uniform,
and as far as possible shall be placed uniformly. All traffic-control devices
and signs shall conform to required state specifications.
§ 70.17 OBEDIENCE TO SIGNALS.
   (A)   It shall be unlawful for the driver of any vehicle to disobey the
signal of any official traffic-control device placed in accordance with the
provisions of this traffic code or of a traffic barrier or sign erected by any
of the public departments or public utilities of the city, or any electric
signal, gate, or watchman at railroad crossings, unless otherwise directed by a
police officer. However, the type and the right to or necessity for such
barrier or sign must be approved by the city.
   (B)   Such sign, signal, marking, or barrier shall have the same authority
as the personal direction of a police officer.
Penalty, see §
70.99
§ 70.18 INTERFERENCE WITH SIGNALS.
   No person shall without authority attempt to or in fact alter, deface,
injure, knock down, or remove any official control device or any railroad sign
or signal, or any inscription, shield, or insignia thereon, or any part
thereof.
Penalty see §
70.99
§ 70.19 UNAUTHORIZED SIGNALS OR MARKINGS.
   (A)   It shall be unlawful for any person to place, maintain, or display on
or in view of any street any unauthorized sign, signal, marking, or device
which purports to be or is an imitation of or resembles an official traffic
device or railroad sign or signal which attempts or purports to direct the
movement of traffic, or which conceals or hides from view or interferes with
the effectiveness of any official control device or any railroad sign or
signal. No person shall place or maintain, nor shall any public authority
permit on any street, any traffic sign or signal bearing any commercial
advertising. Nothing in this section shall be construed as restricting any
public department or public utility of the city in any emergency or temporarily
from marking or erecting any traffic barrier or sign whose placing has been
approved by the city.
   (B)   Every such prohibited sign, signal, or marking is declared to be a
public nuisance and the city is empowered forthwith to remove it or cause it to
be removed.
Penalty, see §
70.99
§ 70.20 DEVICE TO BE LEGIBLE AND IN PROPER POSITION.
   No provision of this traffic code for which signs or any other traffic-
control device is required shall be enforceable against an alleged violator if
at the time and place of the alleged violation the required device was not in
proper position and sufficiently legible to be seen by an ordinarily observant
person.
§ 70.21 TEMPORARY DISREGARD OF DEVICES BY POLICE OFFICERS.
   In an emergency any police officer may at his discretion disregard traffic-
control lights or signals or established regulations in order to facilitate the
movement of traffic.
TRAFFIC CITATIONS
§ 70.55 CITATION IN LIEU OF ARREST.
   Any police officer may issue a citation instead of making an arrest for any
violation of the state vehicle laws or his traffic code where the offense is a
misdemeanor committed in his presence and there are reasonable grounds to
believe that the person cited will appear to answer the charge. The officer
shall take the name, address, and operator's license number of the alleged
violator in writing on a form provided by the city. The citation shall provide
that the defendant shall appear to answer to the charge against him at a place
and time designated therein.
('78 Code, 570.1, § I)
§ 70.56 FAILURE TO COMPLY WITH CITATION.
   If the defendant fails to appear in response to the citation, or if there is
reasonable ground to believe that he will not appear, a complaint may be made
before the District Judge and a warrant shall be issued.
('78 Code, 570.1, § II)
§ 70.99 GENERAL PENALTY.
   (A)   Whoever violates any provision of this traffic code where no other
penalty is specifically provided shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and shall be
fined not less than $20 nor more than $500.
   (B)   Whoever violates one way street regulations as set out in
Chapter 74, Schedule III, shall be guilty of a misdemeanor; and each day of the
continuation thereof shall be a separate and distinct offense for which:
      (1)   Everybody convicted thereof in a court of competent jurisdiction
shall be sentenced to pay a criminal fine not to exceed the maximum amount set
forth in KRS 534.0450(2)(a) or a term of imprisonment not to exceed the maximum
period set forth in KRS 532.090(1), or both; and
      (2)   The offender shall be subject to a civil penalty of $100 for each
offense, which shall be recovered by the city in a civil action in the nature
of debt if not paid by the offender within 30 days after citation for the
violation or other failure to comply with the provisions of this title.
   (C)   Each violation and every failure to comply with the provisions of
speed limit regulations and stop intersection regulations as set forth in
Chapter 74, Schedules I and
II, shall be a violation; and each day of the continuation thereof shall be a
separate and distinct offense for which everybody convicted thereof in a court
of competent jurisdiction shall be sentenced to pay a criminal fine not to
exceed the maximum amount of $250 as set forth in KRS 534.050(2)(c).
(Ord. 68(9-14-94), passed 9-14-94; Am. Ord. 69(9-14-94), passed 9-14-94; Am.
Ord. 71(10-12-94), passed 10-12-94; Am. Ord. 100(10-23-96), passed 10-23-96;
Am. Ord. 109(04-23-97), passed 4-23-97; Am Ord. 155(10-13-99), passed 10-13-99;

Ord. 193(9-25-02), passed 9-25-02)

71.99   Penalty
OPERATION GENERALLY
§ 71.01 OBSTRUCTING TRAFFIC.
   (A)   It shall be unlawful to operate any vehicle or permit it to remain
standing in any street in such manner as to create an obstruction thereof.
   (B)   It shall be unlawful for the operator of any vehicle to enter any
intersection or crosswalk unless there is sufficient space on the other side of
the intersection or crosswalk to accommodate the vehicle without obstructing
the passage of other vehicles or pedestrians, notwithstanding the indication of
any traffic-control signal which may be located at the intersection or
crosswalk.
   (C)   Any intersection deemed by the city to be of special or critical
importance to the movement of traffic shall be marked in such distinctive
manner as to indicate such importance. Should the operator of any vehicle enter
any intersection so marked when there is insufficient room on the other side of
the intersection to accommodate the vehicle, the indication of any traffic-
control signal notwithstanding, he shall be deemed to have violated this
division rather than division (B) above.
Penalty, see §
71.99
§ 71.02 REVERSE OR U TURNS.
   The operator of any vehicle shall not turn such vehicle so as to proceed in
the opposite direction unless such movement can be made in safety without
interfering with other traffic.
(KRS 189.330(8)) Penalty, see §
71.99
§ 71.03 BACKING VEHICLES.
   It shall be unlawful for the operator of any vehicle to back the vehicle at
any intersection for the purpose of executing a turning movement. A vehicle
from any parking position shall be backed by the operator in such manner as to
proceed on the same side of the roadway in the lawful direction of travel.
Penalty, see §
71.99
§ 71.04 VEHICLES CROSSING SIDEWALKS.
   (A)   It shall be unlawful for the operator of any vehicle to drive within
any sidewalk space except at a permanent or temporary driveway or by special
permit from the City Commission, the Chief of Police, or any other authorized
city official.
   (B)   It shall be unlawful for the operator of any vehicle to drive the
vehicle out of any alley, driveway, building, or lot and across a sidewalk, or
its extension across the alley, unless the vehicle has been brought to a
complete stop immediately prior to crossing the sidewalk or its extension. On
entering the roadway from the alley, driveway, or building the operator shall
yield the right-of-way to all vehicles approaching on the roadway. The operator
of any vehicle intending to cross a sidewalk and turn into an alley from the
roadway may do so at low speed and with caution. Penalty, see §
71.99
§ 71.05 SPEED LIMITS.
   (A)   No person shall drive a vehicle upon any public highway or street at a
speed greater than is reasonable and prudent having regard for the traffic, the
condition and use of that highway or street, or so as to endanger the life or
limb or injure the property of any person.
   (B)   Vehicles on public ways and streets in the city shall not exceed the
speed of 35 miles per hour except as set forth in
Chapter 74, Schedule I or except as established by the state.
('78 Code, 530.l, § III (b))
   (C)   Penalty. The fine for violating this speed limit shall be the same as
set forth in the fine schedule of KRS 189.394.
ACCIDENTS
§ 71.15 DUTY OF OPERATOR.
   It shall be the duty of the owner of, operator of, or passenger in any motor
vehicle which is involved in an accident in which any person is injured or
property damaged to stop immediately and ascertain the extent of the injury or
damage and render such assistance as may be needed.
Penalty, see §
71.99
Statutory reference:
   Duty in case of accident, see KRS 189.580
§ 71.16 ACCIDENT REPORT.
   The operator, owner, or passenger involved in an accident resulting in the
injury or death of any person, or an accident in which property is damaged,
shall immediately report the accident or property damage to the Police
Department.
Penalty, see §
71.99
PROHIBITIONS
§ 71.25 INJURY TO STREET BY VEHICLES.
   It shall be unlawful to operate any vehicle so constructed or so loaded as
to do injury to the surface of the street.
Penalty, see §
71.99
§ 71.26 RIGHT-OF-WAY OF EMERGENCY VEHICLES; FOLLOWING EMERGENCY VEHICLES;
DRIVING OVER FIRE HOSE.
   (A) Upon the approach of an emergency vehicle equipped with, and operating,
one or more flashing, rotating, or oscillating red or blue lights visible under
normal conditions from a distance of 500 feet to the front of the emergency
vehicle; or when the driver is giving audible signal by siren, exhaust whistle,
or bell, the driver of every other vehicle shall yield the right-of-way,
immediately drive to a position parallel to, and as close as possible to, the
edge or curb of the highway clear of any intersection, and stop and remain
stopped until the emergency vehicle has passed, except when otherwise directed
by a police officer or firefighter.
   (B) Upon the approach of any emergency vehicle operated in conformity with
the provisions of division (A) above, the operator of every vehicle shall
immediately stop clear of any intersection and shall remain stopped until the
emergency vehicle has passed, unless directed otherwise by a police officer or
firefighter.
   (C) No operator of any vehicle, unless he or she is on official business,
shall follow any emergency vehicle being operated in conformity with the
provisions of division (A) above closer than 500 feet, nor shall he or she
drive into, park the vehicle into, or park the vehicle within the block where
the vehicle has stopped in answer to an emergency call or alarm, unless he or
she is directed otherwise by a police officer or firefighter.
   (D) No vehicle, train, or other equipment shall be driven over any
unprotected hose of a fire department when the hose is laid down on any street,
private driveway, or track for use at any fire or fire alarm unless the fire
department official in command consents that the hose be driven over.
   (E) The provisions of division (F) below shall apply to any driver
approaching a stationary:
      (1)   Emergency vehicle or public safety vehicle, when the emergency
vehicle or public safety vehicle is giving a signal by displaying alternately
flashing yellow, red, red and white, red and blue, or blue lights; or
      (2)   Disabled vehicle, when the disabled vehicle is displaying some type
of warning signal, such as emergency flashers, flares, or retroreflective
signals.
   (F)   The driver of a vehicle that is approaching a vehicle described in
division (E) above shall, while proceeding with due caution:
      (1)   Yield the right-of-way by moving to a lane not adjacent to that of
the vehicle if:
         (a)   The person is driving on a highway having at least four lanes,
with at least two lanes proceeding in the same direction as the approaching
vehicle; and
         (b)   It is possible to make the lane change with due regard to safety
and traffic conditions; or
      (2)   Reduce the speed of the vehicle, maintaining a safe speed to road
conditions, if the road has less than four lanes or if changing lanes would be
impossible or unsafe.
   (G)   This section does not operate to relieve the person who drives an
emergency vehicle from the duty to operate the vehicle with due regard for the
safety of all persons using the highway.
(KRS 189.930) ('78 Code, § 520.5, §§ II, III) Penalty, see §
71.99
§ 71.27 SMOKE EMISSION OR OTHER NUISANCE.
   Every vehicle when on a highway shall be so equipped as to make a minimum of
noise, smoke, or other nuisance, to protect the rights of other traffic, and to
promote the public safety.
(KRS 189.020) Penalty, see §
71.99
PARADES
§ 71.40 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this subchapter the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   "PARADE." Any parade, march, ceremony, show, exhibition, pageant, or
procession of any kind, or any similar display in or on any street, sidewalk,
park, or other public place in the city.
   "PARADE PERMIT." A permit required by this subchapter.
§ 71.41 PERMIT REQUIRED.
   (A)   No person or persons shall engage in, participate in, aid,
form, or start any parade unless a parade permit has been obtained from the
City Commission, the Chief of Police, or any other authorized city official.
   (B)   This subchapter shall not apply to:
      (1)   Funeral processions; or
      (2)   A governmental agency acting within the scope of its functions.
Penalty, see §
71.99
§ 71.42 APPLICATION FOR PERMIT.
   A person seeking issuance of a parade permit shall file an application with
the City Commission, the Chief of Police, or any other authorized city official
on forms provided by that person.
   (A)   Filing period. The application for a parade permit shall be filed not
less than five days or not more than 60 days before the date on which it is
proposed to conduct the parade.
   (B)   The application for a parade permit shall set forth the following
information:
      (1)   The name, address, and telephone number of the person seeking to
conduct the parade;
      (2)   If the parade is proposed to be conducted for, on behalf of, or by
an organization, the name, address, and telephone number of the headquarters of
the organization and of the authorized and responsible heads of the
organization;
      (3)   The name, address, and telephone number of the person who will be
the parade chairman and who will be responsible for its conduct;
      (4)   The date when the parade is to be conducted;
      (5)   The route to be traveled, the starting point, and the termination
point;
      (6)   The approximate number of persons, animals, and vehicles which will
constitute the parade, the type of animals, if any, and the description of the
vehicles;
      (7)   The hours when the parade will start and terminate;
      (8)   A statement as to whether the parade will occupy all or only a
portion of the width of the streets, sidewalk, park, or other public place
proposed to be traversed;
      (9)   The location by street of any assembly area for the parade;
      (10)   The time at which units of the parade will begin to assemble at
any such assembly area or areas;
      (11)   The interval of space to be maintained between units of the
parade;
      (12)   If the parade is designed to be held by, and on behalf of or for,
any person other than the applicant, the applicant for the permit shall file a
communication in writing from the person authorizing the applicant to apply for
the permit on his behalf;
      (13)   Any additional information reasonably necessary to a fair
determination as to whether a permit should issue.
   (C)   There shall be paid at the time of filing an application for a parade
permit a fee in an amount as established by the City Commission.
(Penalty, see §
71.99
§ 71.43 STANDARDS FOR ISSUANCE OF PERMIT.
   The City Commission, the Chief of Police, or any other authorized city
official shall issue a permit when, from a consideration of the application and
from other information obtained, he finds that:
   (A)   The conduct of the parade will not substantially interrupt the safe
and orderly movement of other traffic contiguous to its route;
   (B)   The conduct of the parade will not require the diversion of so great a
number of police officers of the city to properly police the line of movement
and the areas contiguous thereto as to prevent normal police protection to the
city;
   (C)   The conduct of the parade will not require the diversion of so great a
number of ambulances as to prevent normal ambulance service to portions of the
city other than that to be occupied by the proposed line of march and areas
contiguous thereto;
   (D)   The concentration of persons, animals, and vehicles at assembly points
of the parade will not unduly interfere with proper fire and police protection
of, or ambulance service to, areas contiguous to the assembly areas;
   (E)   The conduct of the parade will not interfere with the movement of fire
fighting equipment enroute to a fire;
   (F)   The parade is scheduled to move from its point of origin to its point
of termination expeditiously and without unreasonable delays enroute;
Penalty, see §
71.99
§ 71.44 NOTICE OF REJECTION OF PERMIT.
   The City Commission, the Chief of Police, or any other authorized city
official shall act on the application for a parade permit within three days,
Saturdays, Sundays, and holidays excepted, after filing thereof. If he
disapproves the application, he shall mail to the applicant within the three
days, Saturdays, Sundays, and holidays excepted, after the date on which the
application was filed, a notice of his action stating the reasons for his
denial of the permit.
§ 71.45 APPEAL PROCEDURE WHEN PERMIT DENIED.
   Any person aggrieved shall have the right to appeal the denial of a parade
permit to the City Commission. The appeal shall be taken within 30 days after
notice of denial. The City Commission shall act on the appeal within 30 days
after its receipt.
§ 71.46 ALTERNATIVE PERMIT.
   The City Commission, the Chief of Police, or any other authorized city
official, in denying an application for a parade permit, shall be empowered to
authorize the conduct of the parade on a date, at a time, or over a route
different than that named by the applicant. An applicant desiring to accept an
alternate permit shall file a written notice of his acceptance. An alternate
parade permit shall conform to the requirements of, and shall have the effect
of, a parade permit under this subchapter.
§ 71.47 NOTICE TO CITY AND OTHER OFFICIALS WHEN PERMIT ISSUED.
   Immediately on the issuance of a parade permit, a copy thereof shall be sent
to the following persons:
   (A)   The City Commission;
   (B)   The Legal Counsel for the city;
   (C)   The Fire Chief;
   (D)   The general manager or responsible head of each public utility, the
regular routes of whose vehicles will be affected by the route of the proposed
parade.
§ 71.48 CONTENTS OF PERMIT.
   Each parade permit shall state the following information:
   (A)   Starting time;
   (B)   Minimum speed;
   (C)   Maximum speed;
   (D)   Maximum interval of space to be maintained between the units of the
parade;
   (E)   The portions of the street, sidewalk, park, or other public place to
be traversed that may be occupied by the parade;
   (F)   The maximum length of the parade in miles or fractions thereof;
   (G)   Such other information as is reasonably necessary to the enforcement
of this subchapter.
Penalty, see §
71.99
§ 71.49 DUTIES OF PERMITTEE.
   A permittee hereunder shall comply with all permit directions and conditions
and with all applicable laws and ordinances. The parade chairman or other
person heading or leading the activity shall carry the parade permit on his
person during the conduct of the parade.
Penalty, see §
71.99
§ 71.50 PUBLIC CONDUCT DURING PARADES.
   (A)   Interference. No person shall unreasonably hamper, obstruct, impede,
or interfere with any parade or parade assembly or with any person, vehicle, or
animal participating or used in a parade.
   (B)   Driving through parades. No driver of a vehicle except a police car or
other emergency vehicle shall drive between the vehicles or persons comprising
a parade when such vehicles or persons are in motion and are conspicuously
designated as a parade.
   (C)   Parking on parade route. The City Commission, the Chief of Police, or
any other authorized city official shall have the authority, when reasonably
necessary, to prohibit or restrict the parking of vehicles along a street or
other public thoroughfare or part thereof constituting a part of the route of a
parade. Signs shall be posted to such effect, and it shall be unlawful for any
person to park or leave unattended any vehicle in violation thereof. No person
shall be liable for parking on a street or other public thoroughfare unless
signs have been posted in accordance with this division.
Penalty, see §
71.99
§ 71.51 REVOCATION OF PERMIT.
   The city shall have the authority to revoke a parade permit issued hereunder
on application of the standards for issuance as herein set forth.
TRUCKS AND COMMERCIAL VEHICLES
§ 71.70 RESTRICTIONS ON TRUCKS.
   (A)   It shall be unlawful for any truck over 36,000 pounds gross weight
(including the load) to travel on or use any of the streets of the city as a
thoroughfare, except in connection with and in the ordinary course of business,
such as loading, unloading, or performing a service for a resident or business
of the city.
   (B)   This section shall not apply to trucks traveling on state or county
roads within the city.
('78 Code, 520.3, § I) Penalty, see §
71.99
§ 71.71 RESTRICTIONS ON COMMERCIAL VEHICLES.
   (A)   For the purpose of this section the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
      (1)   "BUYER." A person who buys or contracts to buy goods.
      (2)   "COMMERCIAL VEHICLE." Any truck, truck tractor, trailer or semi-
trailer, other than a recreational vehicle.
      (3)   "CONSTRUCTION SITE." Any lot, parcel or tract of land for which
there is a valid, unexpired Taylor Mill building permit conspicuously posted
thereon.
      (4)   "FARM." Any parcel or tract of land which consists of at least five
(5) contiguous acres, which is used for agricultural or horticultural purposes
including, without limitation, livestock and livestock products, poultry and
poultry products, grain, hay, soybeans, tobacco, pastures and other crops,
timber, orchards, fruit, vegetables, flowers and ornamental plants, along with
buildings and other structures necessary therefor, including, without
limitation, dwellings for the owners and operators thereof.
      (5)   "GOODS." Any property which is both moveable and tangible.
      (6)   "RECREATIONAL VEHICLE." Has the same meaning therefor provided in
KRS 219.320(8).
      (7)   "SELLER." A person who sells or contracts to sell goods.
      (8)   "SEMI-TRAILER." A wheeled vehicle with a load capacity of over
1,500 pounds, which is designed to have its front end supported and pulled by a
truck or truck tractor, as defined herein.
      (9)   "STREET." Any street or highway other than those streets or
highways maintained by Kenton County or the Commonwealth of Kentucky.
      (10)   "TRAILER." A wheeled vehicle with a load capacity of over 1,000
pounds, which is designed to be pulled by a, truck or truck tractor, as defined
herein, but supported by its own wheels, independent of any other support.
      (11)   "TRUCK." Any motor vehicle with a declared gross weight in excess
of 6,000 pounds, other than emergency vehicles of the city.
      (12)   "TRUCK TRACTOR." Any motor vehicle designed to pull and support
the front end of a semi-trailer.
   (B)   No person shall cause or permit the operation or location of a
commercial vehicle upon any portion of any street in the city except for the
purpose of delivery of goods from a seller to a buyer who is either a resident
or owner of real estate which is contiguous to any portion of the street.
   (C)   Nobody shall conspire, promote, cause, permit, allow, aid, assist,
encourage or engage in the location of any parked commercial vehicle outside of
a garage or other enclosure, on any lot or parcel of real estate in the City
other than a farm, or construction site, or any public right-of-way abutting
thereon, unless such commercial vehicle is being used for the purpose of the
receipt or delivery of tangible items to or from a resident or owner of such
parcel of real estate, other than the owner or operator of such commercial
vehicle.
   (D)   A violation of this section occurs upon any non-compliance with any
provision of this section, by either act or omission; and each and every
separate non-continuing occurrence thereof, and each and every day of any
continuing occurrence thereof is a separate violation of this section.
(Ord. 1-3-83, passed - -83; Am. Ord. 167(10-25-00), passed 10-25-00) Penalty,
see §
71.99
§ 71.72 RESTRICTIONS ON COMMERCIAL TRUCKS.
   (A)   Definitions. As used herein, the following words and phrases have the
meanings indicated for them.
      (1)   "ANYBODY." Any human being, any organization, or combination
thereof, in the form of a corporation, partnership, joint venture,
unincorporated association or otherwise.
      (2)   "COMMERCIAL TRUCK." Any motor vehicle with a gross vehicle weight
rating (GVWR) of more than 10,000 pounds.
      (3)   "MOTOR VEHICLE." Any wheeled vehicle propelled by any means other
than gravity or muscular power.
      (4)   "NOBODY." No human being, no organization, or combination thereof,
in the form of a corporation, partnership, joint venture, unincorporated
association or otherwise.
      (5)   "SIGN." A sign designed, made, installed and maintained according
to the specifications of the Bureau of Highways of the Transportation Cabinet
of the Commonwealth of Kentucky.
   (B)   Sign location. The Public Works Department of the city shall cause
signs prohibiting commercial trucks to be installed, located and maintained at
the following locations:
      (1)   Within the northerly side of the right-of-way of Blackstone Court,
at its intersection with the right-of-way of Pride Parkway, so that the sign is
facing motor vehicle traffic proceeding in an easterly direction on Blackstone
Court.
      (2)   Within the easterly side of the right-of-way of Maple Ridge Drive
at its intersection with the right-of-way of McCowan Drive, so that the sign is
facing motor vehicle traffic proceeding in an easterly direction on McCowan
Drive.
   (C)   Prohibition. Nobody shall cause, promote, aid, assist, encourage,
allow or engage in the operation of any commercial truck on either:
      (1)   Any portion of Blackstone Court; or
      (2)   Any portion of McCowan Drive, between Maple Ridge Drive and
Blackstone Court.
(Ord. 317(01-11-2017), passed 01-11-17) Penalty, see §
71.99
§ 71.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Whoever violates any provision of this chapter for which no other
penalty is specifically provided shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and fined not
less than $20 nor more than $500.
   (B)   Any person who violates §
71.26 shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and fined not less than $60 nor more
than $500, or be imprisoned in the county jail for not more than 30 days, or
both. (KRS 189.993(8))
   (C)   (1)   Each separate violation of §
71.71 is hereby classified as a criminal offense and made a misdemeanor, for
which there is hereby imposed a criminal fine, not to exceed the maximum of
$500, as set forth in KRS 534.050(2), or a term of imprisonment not to exceed
the maximum period of 12 months, as set forth in KRS 532.090(1), or both.
      (2)   Each separate violation of §
71.71 is hereby classified as a civil offense, for which:
         (a)   The maximum civil fine required by KRS 65.8808(2)(b)1. that may
be imposed for each separate violation of §
71.71, is hereby established as $500;
         (b)   The specific civil fine required by KRS 65.8808(2)(b)2., that
will be imposed for each separate offense and violation of §
71.71 if the person who has committed the violation and offense does not
contest a citation therefor, is hereby established as $100; and
         (c)   An enforcement officer may, in lieu of immediately issuing a
civil citation therefor, give notice that the violation of §
71.71 shall be remedied within a specific period of time.
(Am. Ord. 167(10-25-00), passed 10-25-00)
   (D)   Each violation and every other failure to comply with the provisions
of §
71.72 shall be a violation; and each day of the continuation thereof shall be a
separate and distinct offense for which everybody convicted thereof in a court
of competent jurisdiction shall be sentenced to pay a criminal fine not to
exceed the maximum amount of $250, as set forth in KRS 534.050(2)(c).
(Am. Ord. 317(01-11-2017), passed 01-11-17)
